+Jamison Brereton

45 (665)
Indra (except 1: Agni and Indra)
Tri┼Ыoka K─Бс╣Зva
42 verses: g─Бyatr─л, arranged in trcas ╠е
The hymn begins and ends with a tr╠еca marked by a refrain (vss. 1тАУ3 and 40тАУ42). The tr╠еca division can otherwise be faint, and in several instances seems to contravene groupings of verse by content (see esp. vss. 36тАУ39). The Anukramaс╣З─л attributes the hymn to a certain Tri┼Ыoka, but this name has probably been plucked from verse 30.
The first two verses establish a ritual mise-en-sce╠Аne, but we quickly move into the martial and competitive mode that prevails in most of the rest of this long hymn. Familiar chords are struck: Indra is exhorted to destroy enemies in various fero cious ways (e.g., vs. 8) and to parcel out their goods to us (e.g., vs. 15), to drink our soma and aid our efforts (e.g., vs. 14), and to give us rich gifts (e.g., vs. 12), and he is praised for his past deeds (see esp. vss. 25тАУ30).
But the hymn also has several unusual features. The poet expresses a remarkable degree of apprehension about the exercise of IndraтАЩs powers and fear that they may be turned against him and his comrades. Although a certain amount of such senti ment (as in the beginning of vs. 10) is not rare in Indra hymns, the sequence of verses 31тАУ35, which begins with a plea to Indra not to do what he has in mind and seeks to accomplish, a sharp reversal of the usual request, depicts men in fear of being IndraтАЩs targetsтАФor perhaps even just of witnessing his terrifying hyper-power (see vss. 32, 35)тАФand begging for his mercy. Already in verse 19 they expressed worry about their shaky relationship with Indra, and the poet speaks of their тАЬoffensesтАЭ in verse 34, a term more at home in an ─Аdityan context.
Even more striking are two snatches of dialogue, which bookend the hymn: the first two verses of the second tr╠еca (vss. 4тАУ5) and the first two verses of the penul timate tr╠еca (vss. 37тАУ38). In the first pair the just-born Indra takes up a bow and asks his mother about potential enemies, and she replies with what appears to be a proverbial expression assuring him of his ultimate victory. (This scene has a close parallel in VIII.77.1тАУ2.) In verses 37тАУ38 it seems (the verses are quite obscure and uncontextualized) that Indra and the Maruts exchange slangy insults: in 37 Indra reproaches the Maruts (not named but identified by one of their epithets) for not honoring their partnership by even thinking of abandoning him, while they reply in 38 by suggesting that he should have thought of that before, when he was hogging the soma. The unspoken context is the well-known episode when all the gods but the Maruts abandon Indra before the Vr╠еtra battle (see, e.g., VIII.96.7, using some of the same vocabulary), and the Maruts later demand from Indra a share in the soma sacrifice because they stood by him (see especially the dialogue hymn I.165). This intriguingly deracinated exchange seems to have been suggested to the poet by verse 36, in which he himself hopes not to be deprived of a comrade. If Indra himself could find himself deserted by his friends, how much more conceivable such a situa tion is for a mere mortal. This theme of comradeship was announced in the refrain to the first tr╠еca (vss. 1тАУ3) and arises several times elsewhere in the hymn (vss. 16, 18).
Though the hymn does not have a clear structureтАФand its length would have made such a structure difficult to apprehend in a performance situationтАФthe themes and concerns that keep surfacing give some sense of unity, and the two little dialogues at the two ends of the hymn grab the attention.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThose (sages) who kindle Agni, those of whom the ever-young Indra is the friend, continually spreadthe sacred grass.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Those who kindle the fire and strew the ritual grass in due order,
of whom Indra is the youthful comrade,

+Griffith

HITHERWARD! they who light flame and straightway trim the sacred grass.
Whose Friend is Indra ever young.

+Grassmann

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬYour strong mother answered you, “he who wishes your enmity fights as the elephant in the mountain”.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Elephant: apsaс╕е = person nal charms, teeth (RV 1.124.7), beauty (RV 5.80.6; here, a beautiful elephant; or, is itthe cloud which covers the earth and the mountains (i.e. vс╣Ыtra)?

+Jamison Brereton

She, the strong one [/┼Ъavas─л], replied to you: тАЬLike a wasp at a mountain he will fight,
who desires rivalry with you.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton Notes

┼Ъavas─л is taken by many as the name of IndraтАЩs mother, but there is no particular reason not to take it in its lexical sense, referring to the same woman.

The Pp. text divides the beginning of b into gir─Б╠Бv ├бpso, with the second word the s-stem ├бpsas- тАШbreastтАЩ, a word otherwise used of Uс╣гas (I.124.7, V.80.6). But even in a proverbial expression such as this seems to be, where semantic latitude is to be expected, тАЬlike a/the breast/chest at a mountainтАЭ (or Geldner тАЬWie mit der Brust gegen den Berg …,тАЭ taking ├бpsaс╕е as a truncated instr. *├бpsas─Б) doesnтАЩt make any sense. Oldenberg suggests a different word division: gir─Б╠Бv├бpso, with the latter being the word for тАШwaspтАЩ found elsewhere in Indo-European, though not directly in Indo-Aryan (except, quite possibly, in I.181.8); see EWA s.v. v├бpsas-. This does allow sense to be made of the expression: the extraordinary size difference between a wasp and a mountain dooms the wasp, but wasps are notoriously belligerent and therefore willing to take on any opponent, however unlikely they are to defeat it. In the same way, anyone who is foolhardy enough to take on Indra will ensure certain defeat for himself.

+Grassmann

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWhen Indra, the warrior, goes to battle, desirous of gallant steeds, he is the foremost of the lords ofchariots.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

When the setter of contests drives to the contest in search of good horses, Indra
is the best charioteer of charioteers.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The published translation may not make it clear that I think that Indra is also the тАЬsetter of contestsтАЭ of the subordinate clause.

+Griffith

What time the Warrior Indra goes to battle, borne by noble steeds,
Best of all charioteers is he.

+Geldner

Wenn der streitbare Indra in den Streit zieht, der sch├╢ne Rosse gern hat, der beste der Wagenlenker,

+Grassmann

Wenn Indra in den Wettkampf geht, kampfwirkend, sch├╢ner Rosse froh, So ist der Lenker bester er.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThunderer, smite all your enemies that you may be scattered– be to us a most abundant benefactor.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Rip apart all attackers, mace-bearer, as if into (a million) pieces. Become the one who most receives our praises.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Assuming that the syntagm of the simile is v├нс╣гvag y├бth─Б тАЬas if v├нс╣гvak,тАЭ that is, тАЬas if asunder,тАЭ I have slightly reconfigured the expression to conform to an English idiom. Geldner seems to take the y├бth─Б as expressing purpose, тАЬdass sie zerschellenтАЭ (be smashed to pieces) but I do not understand how v├нс╣гvak can be configured as a verb.

Note the alliteration v├н с╣г├║ v├н┼Ыv─Б … v├бjrin v├нс╣гvag тАж vс╣Ыha, esp. v├н с╣г├║ v├н┼Ыv─Б …

v├нс╣гvag.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

There is no expressed referent in this verse, and Grassmann (s.v. ├б┼Ыv─Бvant-, etc.) indicates that it is тАЬweтАЭ of vs. 10. However, Geldner supplies тАЬsoma drops,тАЭ esp. on the strength of VIII.49.4 and the fact that viv├бkс╣гana- is always used of soma. This seems correct. The question is the meaning and root affiliation of viv├бkс╣гana-. Geldner tr.

тАШredselig machendтАЩ, connecting it thus with тИЪvac, while I prefer to take it to тИЪvakс╣г тАШbecome / make strongтАЩ, as a transitive -ana-nominal, beside v├бkс╣гaс╣Зa- also тАШstrengtheningтАЩ. The connection with тИЪvakс╣г is asserted by Oldenberg ad X.21.1 (fld. by AiG II.2.198). See also EWA s.v. VAKс╣в, esp. p. 487; he does not decide.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWhenever, repairing to you in our distress, we offer our praises, attend to us, Indra, as a giver of cattle.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

For even though weтАЩve thought that weтАЩve been going a wayward course to you,
still become for us a giver of cows, Indra.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The logical relation between the subordinate clause (ab) and main clause (c) is somewhat indirect. The point seems to be that though we think that our behavior towards Indra has not been entirely straightforward and proper, we hope that he will continue to be generous to us despite our failings.

+Griffith

When even now, when we have been in trouble, we have thought of thee,
O Indra, give us gifts of kine.

+Geldner

Obschon wir ja des Glaubens sind, einen Fehltritt gegen dich begangen zu haben, so sei uns, Indra, doch ein Kuhschenker!

+Grassmann

Denn wenn wir je dir waren werth als die, die deine Wege gehn, So schenke, Indra, Rinder uns.

+Elizarenkova

+Jamison Brereton Notes

mah├й was mistakenly omitted in the published translation Substitute тАЬto great generosity.тАЭ I follow Oldenberg in taking g├│par─лс╣Зas─Б as standing for -─Бс╕е, nom. pl. to a thematic stem, rather than, with Geldner (and Pp.), as -─Б and instr. sg. of the s-stem. In the simplex both p├бr─лс╣Зas- and par─лс╣Зas├б- exist, though the latter occurs only once (IX.97.9), where it is indirectly associated with cows/milk. Oldenberg points out that soma is generally the subject of тИЪmand (as in 14b mandantu тАж ├нndavaс╕е), and taking g├│par─лс╣Зas─Б(с╕е) here as modifying a plural form of soma drinks or drops would save having to supply another element in the instrumental. However, GeldnerтАЩs interpretation does have in its favor that the more common simplex is p├бr─лс╣Зas- and that it is regularly found in the instrumental. ### 25-27 The proclamation of IndraтАЩs deeds called for in 25c is presumably contained in the following two verses.

+Grassmann

Hier soll’n mit milchgef├╝lltem Trank sie dich zu reichem Lohn erfreun, Den See trink aus dem B├╝ffel gleich.

рд╕рд╛рдпрдг-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрдореН

рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдХрджреНрд░реБрд╡рдГ рдХрджреНрд░реБрдирд╛рдордХрд╕реНрдпрд░реНрд╖реЗрдГ рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐рдирдВ рд╕реБрддрдореН рдЕрднрд┐рд╖реБрддрдВ рд╕реЛрдордореН рдЕрдкрд┐рдмрддреН рдкреАрддрд╡рд╛рдиреН ред рд╕рд╣рд╕реНрд░рдмрд╛рд╣реНрд╡реЗ рд╕рд╣рд╕реНрд░рдмрд╛рд╣реЛрдГ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдВрд╢реНрдЪрд╛рд╣рдиреНрдирд┐рддрд┐ рд╢реЗрд╖рдГ ред рдЕрддреНрд░ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрдирд╡рд╕рд░реЗ рдкреМрдВрд╕реНрдпрдореН рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рд╡реАрд░реНрдпрдореН рдЕрджреЗрджрд┐рд╖реНрдЯ рдЕрджреАрдкреНрдпрдд рее

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬIndra drank the Soma offering of Kadru, (he smote the enemies) of the thousand-armed; there did hismight shine forth.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Kadravaс╕е = belonging to a с╣Ыс╣гi named Kadru; or, genitive, or abl. of Kadru, the well-known motherof the n─Бgas;

Sahasrab─Бhve = battle

+Jamison Brereton

Indra drank the pressed (soma) of Kadr┼л for that which possesses a thousand-arms [=battle?].
Then he displayed his own masculine power.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Grassmann takes sah├бsrab─Бhve (with distraction, -b─Бhuve) as belonging to a ustem and as a poetic synonym for тАШbattleтАЩ. I find this suggestion quite attractive, though this type of kenning is somewhat unusual for the RV. Geldner and Oldenberg (see also EWA s.v. b─Бh├║-; Mayrhofer PN) take it as a thematized -b─Бhva- in the locative as a PN (Geldner: тАЬbei Sahasrab─БhvaтАЭ). Though GrassmannтАЩs interpretation gives the richer semantics, the problem is of course that the dative sg. should be -b─Бhave, not -b─Бh u ve. AiG III.139 also identifies it as a thematic locative, but allows a lexical meaning тАЬin der tausendarmigen Schlacht,тАЭ flg. Sommer). I still think it may be a dative, with the alternative -ve ending (e.g., p├б┼Ыve beside pa┼Ы├бve), but a locative with lexical value is also possible.

+Griffith

In battle of a thousand arms Indra drank Kadru’s Soma juice:
There he displayed his manly might.

+Geldner

Indra trank der Kadru Saft bei Sahasrabahva. Da offenbarte er seine Mannesst├дrke.

+Grassmann

Es trank den Soma aus dem Fass Indra zur tausendarm’gen Schlacht, Da wies er seine Manneskraft.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWell-knowing those (sacrificial) deeds of Turva┼Ыa and Yadu, he overcame Anhav─Бyya in battle.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Turva┼Ыa, Yadu: the names are associated in RV 1.36.18, 54.6; 174.9;

Ahnavayya: he prevailed indisputably inbattle

+Jamison Brereton

This is real: having obtained at Turva┼ЫaтАЩs and YaduтАЩs what is not to be spurned [=soma],
he came through to victory by his labor.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner takes v├нd─Бnaс╕е as belonging to тИЪvid тАШknowтАЩ and construes it with the preceding PNs: тАЬDas ist wahr, bei Turva┼Ыa und Yadu bekannt.тАЭ It is true that the participle v├нd─Бna- ordinarily belongs to тИЪvid тАШknowтАЩ, but it is usually passive and appears with a predicate, тАЬknown as X.тАЭ The idiom envisioned here, тАЬknown to,тАЭ IтАЩm not at all sure is a Sanskrit expression, though it works well in German and English. I therefore take the participle as belonging to тИЪvid тАШfindтАЩ, whose middle generally means тАШacquireтАЩ, with the soma тАЬnot to be spurnedтАЭ (ahnav─Бyy├бm) as object. Turva┼Ыa and Yadu offer soma to the gods elsewhere; cf. VIII.9.14 im├й s├│m─Бso ├бdhi turv├б┼Ыe y├бdau. Geldner takes ahnav─Бyy├бm with vy ─Б╠Аnaс╣н (тАЬhat er nicht Abzustreitendes erreichtтАЭ), which prevents him from construing that verb with turv├бс╣Зe as it is in the parallel he himself cites (VIII.12.19 ├бdh─Б yaj├▒─Б╠Бya turv├бс╣Зe vy─Б╠Аna┼Ыuс╕е). His rendering of the last two words of the p─Бda as purpose infinitival clause (тАЬdass der fromme Dienst triumphiereтАЭ) involves what seems to me a dubious construal of ┼Ы├бmi.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWhatever you undertake in your exhilaration, whatever you purpose in your mind or are thinking tobestow– O Indra, do it not, but bless us.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Do it not, for you have done it for us– only make us happy

+Jamison Brereton

What you take on, have in mind, and, becoming exhilarated, set out to accomplish,
donтАЩt do that, Indra. Have mercy!

+Jamison Brereton Notes

For the odd sentiments of this verse and what follows, see the introduction. Both Geldner and Oldenberg supply an object to the first verb (dadhiс╣гe), an object drawn from ritual (Geldner тАЬdas Opfer,тАЭ Oldenberg тАЬLob u. degl., Somatr├дnkeтАЭ), but this seems unduly restrictive.

I think that the poet is apprehensive about the consequences of whatever Indra might undertake.

+Griffith

Whate’er thy plan or purpose be, whate’er, in transport, thou wouldst do,
Do it not, Indra, but be kind.

+Geldner

Da├Я du das Opfer empfangen hast und dich noch bedenkst, wenn du berauscht bist, und es doch bekommen m├╢chtest, das tu nicht, Indra; sei barmherzig!

+Grassmann

Was, Indra, du ersinnst und thust, was du erfreut uns schenken willst, Das schaff nicht fort von hier, sei hold.

+Elizarenkova

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

An anser to с╣Ыcas 34 and 35

+Jamison Brereton

[Indra to Maruts:] тАЬYou young bucksтАФwho, (as if) unpaired, has said, as comrade to comrade,
тАШI will leave (you)тАЩ? Who retreats from us?тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton Notes

On the basis both of the content of the verse and the use of the voc. mary─Бс╕е, I consider this verse to be IndraтАЩs address to the Maruts. The plural of mary├б in all clear cases refers to the Maruts. And in VIII.96.7-8 the Maruts address Indra, reminding him that all the other gods but them deserted him, using the same тИЪ─лс╣г тАШshrink fromтАЩ as is found here.

Geldner takes ├бmithitaс╕е as тАЬohne ZankтАЭ (without a quarrel), but I think it refers instead to IndraтАЩs potentially friendless state –тАШunpairedтАЩ - a fear expressed by the poet in the immediately preceding verse (36). The hypothetical speaker still has a comrade (s├бkh─Б s├бkh─Бyam), but, like one unpaired, threatens to say to this comrade тАЬIтАЩm leaving.тАЭ The form jah─Б╠Бis taken by Geldner (and others) as a 3rd sg. pf. to тИЪh─Б and therefore, implicitly, a precious example of a 3rd sg. pf. to a long-─Б root without -au ending.

However, Oldenberg very persuasively suggests that it is a 1st sg. subjunctive in the direct speech introduced by abrav─лt. Although to the reduplicated present of тИЪh─Б we would expect accent on the reduplication (*j├бh─Б), Oldenberg argues that the fluctuation of accent in IIIrd class presents makes the accent irrelevant. I would alternatively suggest that it could be a subjunctive to the perfect stem. See OldenbergтАЩs extensive discussion of the various previous proposals about this form.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬShowerer (of benefits), when the ready Soma was effused, you did devour much, without stint, rushingdown like a gameste.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Asinvan = na badhnan; RV. 7.39.6: apratibadhn─Бn, not hindering the desires of mortals

+Jamison Brereton

[Maruts to Indra:] тАЬHey bull. SoтАФwhen (the soma) was pressed, being insatiable you consumed a lot,
sashaying around the lower depths like a guy with тАШthe dog-killerтАЩ [=the winning throw at dice].тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton Notes

I consider this verse the MarutsтАЩ insulted response to IndraтАЩs insults, couched in a very slangy register. The first sign of this speech level is the voc. are (to ar├н- тАШstrangerтАЩ), a vocative not otherwise found in the RV, but remember the P─Бli and Pkt. тАЬinterjectionsтАЭ are, ale, clearly derived from this voc. (Thieme, Fremdl. 3-4), as well as the famous shibboleth he тАШlavo of ┼ЪB III.2.1.23, consisting of an l-form of the plural voc. of this word in MIA guise (see EWA, KEWA s.v.). Its use as a shibboleth and with an l-form suggests popular speech.

Note also the lengthened voc. vс╣Ыс╣гabh─Б (also in 22a). Lengthened vocatives are quite rare in the RV; AiG III.96-97 cites only these two forms, but remarks that pluti vocatives were surely a feature of living speech, found in the Br─Бhmaс╣Зas and in P─Бli and the Pr─Бkrits. The use of the well-known gambling term svaghn─л╠Бalso marks the speech as low register. The substance of the MarutsтАЩ counter-accusations is that Indra greedily drank up the soma offered to him below (that is, among men). IтАЩve used the expression тАЬlower depthsтАЭ to refer to the louche aspects of a gambling place (and also possibly to the depression in the ground where the dicing happens). Indra carried on arrogantly and without sharing the soma, but then, they say, when he got into a jam in the Vrtra ╠е battle he suddenly remembered he had pals and upbraided them for desertion.

+Griffith

Hero, insatiate enjoy this Soma juice so near to thee,
Even as a hunter rushing down.

+Geldner

Wahrlich, du Bulle, du hast zum Soma viel verzehrt ohne zu kauen, wie ein Falschspieler unterschlagend.

+Grassmann

Beim Soma, nimmersatter Stier, der recht dir ist, verschlangst du viel, Dem Spieler gleich, als her du kamst.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬI draw here your two steeds, harnessed to a beauiful chariot and yoked by hymns, since you givewealth to the br─Бhmaс╣Зas.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

I hold onto these two fallow bays of yours, yoked by speech, along with their chariot,
so that you will give to the formulators.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Unfortunately this last verse of the tс╣Ыca does not seem to have any connection with the foregoing Indra-Marut dialogue. The “I” is presumably not a Marut, but the poet or other ritual officiant, and itтАЩs difficult to know how his holding on to the horses will bring about IndraтАЩs gifts. Is he holding them hostage, as it were, not allowing them to leave the ritual ground and return to heaven (recall the тАЬFallowbay-yoking libationтАЭ that ends I.61-63 and sends Indra and his horses back home at the end of the sacrifice) until Indra distributes the goods? Or is he helpfully holding them to leave IndraтАЩs hands free? Given the aggressive tone of the previous two verses, I favor the former idea.

+Wilson
English translation:

+Jamison Brereton

will knowтАФ
the craved good thingтАФbring that here.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

vi┼Ыv├бm─Бnuс╣гa- should, by accent, be a bahuvr─лhi; it is also difficult to separate from vi┼Ыv├бmanus- in the next hymn (VIII.46.17). However, most interpretors take it implicitly as a karmadh─Бraya: Grassmann тАШdie ganze MenschenscharтАЩ, Geldner тАШjedermannтАЩ, and Wackernagel (AiG II.1.266) explicitly identifies it as a tatpuruс╣гa with irregular accent (тАШGesamtheit der MenschenтАЩ). But this seems unnecessary: m─Б╠Бnuс╣гa- regularly modifies j├бna- (so тАШhuman raceтАЩ / or тАШfolk consisting of the descendants of ManuтАЩ), and here we can supply an underlying j├бna-, modified by the compound, hence тАШ(races) consisting of all the people of ManuтАЩ. The published translation seems to reflect the tatpuruс╣гa interpretation because the more literal tr. is simply too awkward.

+Griffith

+Geldner

Wovon jedermann Kunde haben soll, von dem in F├╝lle von dir Geschenkten, das begehrenswerte Gut, das bring mit!

+Grassmann

Das reiche, was die ganze Welt bezeuget als von dir geschenkt, Das Gut bring’ her, das wir ersehnt.

+Elizarenkova
